reference PyTorch source (the prompt the agent sees)
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig

class Model(torch.nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, model_name, config):
        super().__init__()
        self.model_name = model_name
        self.config = config
        self.model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(self.model_name, config=self.config)

    def forward(self, x):
        return self.model(x).logits

model_name = "facebook/bart-large"
config = AutoConfig.from_pretrained(model_name)
vocab_size = config.vocab_size
sequence_length = 32
batch_size = 1024

def get_inputs():
    inputs = torch.randint(0, vocab_size, (batch_size, sequence_length))
    return [inputs]

def get_init_inputs():
    return [model_name, config]

This is the main source of speedup for small batch/seq in inference. In `BartDecoderLayer`, the operations are: 1. Self-attention: - Layernorm - Q, K, V linear - Reshape for heads - Compute causal mask (can be precomputed) - Scaled dot-product attention (matmul, softmax, dropout, matmul) - Out projection - Dropout - Residual add 2. For a layer, there are ~20+ kernel launches. Over 12 layers, that's 240+ kernels. Each kernel launch takes ~5-10 microseconds. Total launch overhead: 1-2 milliseconds. The actual compute might be 10-20 milliseconds. So reducing launch overhead by 1ms might give 5-10% speedup. Not huge. In older versions of `transformers`, `BartAttention` computes attention manually: ```python query_states = self.q_proj(hidden_states) * self.scaling key_states = self._shape(self.k_proj(hidden_states), -1, bsz) value_states = self._shape(self.v_proj(hidden_states), -1, bsz) proj_shape = (bsz * self.num_heads, -1, self.head_dim) query_states = self._shape(query_states, tgt_len, bsz).view(*proj_shape) key_states = key_states.view(*proj_shape) value_states = value_states.view(*proj_shape) src_len = key_states.size(1) attn_weights = torch.bmm(query_states, key_states.transpose(1, 2)) # add causal mask attn_weights = nn.functional.softmax(attn_weights, dim=-1) attn_probs = nn.functional.dropout(attn_weights, p=self.dropout, training=self.training) attn_output = torch.bmm(attn_probs, value_states) ``` This is the classic approach. It does `bmm` for Q@K^T, then `softmax`, then `dropout`, then `bmm` for attn@V. It might not call the fused `scaled_dot_product_attention` if the transformers version is old. If we write a kernel that takes `hidden_states` and `W_qkv`, computes Q, K, V, then does attention, then projects out, all in one kernel, that would be a huge win for memory bandwidth. But implementing a batched multi-head attention CUDA kernel from scratch is difficult, but not impossible if we reuse PyTorch's dispatch or write a simple one. However, the shape is `M=1024*16=16384` batches, each doing a `32x64` times `64x32` matmul. That's many small GEMMs. A custom kernel might not beat cuBLAS's batched GEMM, but fusing the softmax and dropout could help. Alternatively, the `attn_weights` tensor has shape `[16384, 32, 32]`. For each batch element, softmax over 32 elements is tiny. cuDNN/cuBLAS handles it well. Fusing it might reduce memory traffic but not compute time. I think the cleanest approach given the constraints is to write the full forward pass in C++ ATen. Let me draft this. For BART decoder layer, exact ATen operations: ```cpp // Self-attention auto residual = hidden; hidden = at::native_layer_norm(hidden, {hidden.size(-1)}, layernorm_weight, layernorm_bias, eps).output; auto q = at::addmm(q_bias, hidden, q_weight.t()); auto k = at::addmm(k_bias, hidden, k_weight.t()); auto v = at::addmm(v_bias, hidden, v_weight.t()); // Reshape for multi-head attention q = q.reshape({B, S, H, D/H}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); // (B, H, S, D/H) k = k.reshape({B, S, H, D/H}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); v = v.reshape({B, S, H, D/H}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); // Attention auto scores = at::matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)) / sqrt(D/H); scores = scores + causal_mask; scores = at::softmax(scores, -1); auto attn = at::matmul(scores, v); // Reshape and project attn = attn.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({B, S, D}); auto out = at::addmm(out_bias, attn, out_weight.t()); hidden = residual + out; // FFN residual = hidden; hidden = at::native_layer_norm(hidden, {hidden.size(-1)}, ffn_layernorm_weight, ffn_layernorm_bias, eps).output; auto ffn1 = at::addmm(fc1_bias, hidden, fc1_weight.t()); ffn1 = at::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = at::addmm(fc2_bias, ffn1, fc2_weight.t()); hidden = residual + ffn2; ``` For the causal mask, BART uses a mask where future positions are masked with a large negative value. In PyTorch, this is typically computed as: ```python causal_mask = torch.triu(torch.ones(S, S), diagonal=1) * -10000.0 ``` For a single sequence shape (S, S), we can broadcast it to (B, H, S, S). The tolerance is 1e-4 absolute/relative, which is quite generous for fp32. Small differences in the mask or softmax implementation are unlikely to matter much. But I should aim for exactness. For `at::softmax`, PyTorch uses the numerically stable implementation: ```python x_max = x.max(dim=-1, keepdim=True) e_x = torch.exp(x - x_max) result = e_x / e_x.sum(dim=-1, keepdim=True) ``` `at::softmax` in C++ should produce identical results. For `at::gelu`, BART uses the standard GELU. In PyTorch, `F.gelu` uses the `erf` formulation: `0.5 * x * (1 + erf(x / sqrt(2)))`. `at::gelu` should match. For layer norm, `at::native_layer_norm` should match `nn.LayerNorm`. For `at::addmm`, it computes `beta * input + alpha * (mat1 @ mat2)`. For bias addition: `at::addmm(bias, input, weight.t())` should match `F.linear(input, weight, bias)`. Given all this, using ATen ops should give bit-exact or near-bit-exact results with the reference. Let me now write the actual code. Let me include a custom CUDA kernel for the attention mechanism. For sequence length 32, this could be very efficient. ### Custom Attention Kernel Design For each (batch_idx, head_idx), we want to compute: ```python # Q, K, V are each (D,) per position # scores[i][j] = dot(Q[i], K[j]) / sqrt(head_dim) # attn[i] = sum_j(softmax(scores)[i][j] * V[j]) ``` Input to kernel: - q: (B, H, S, Dh) where Dh = D/H - k: (B, H, S, Dh) - v: (B, H, S, Dh) - output: (B, H, S, Dh) Grid: (B, H) blocks Threads: Let's use 256 threads per block Algorithm per block: 1. Load Q into shared memory: `__shared__ float q_sm[32][64]` - 32 positions * 64 floats = 2048 floats = 8KB 2. Load K into shared memory: 8KB 3. Load V into shared memory: 8KB 4. Compute Q @ K^T in registers/scratchpad: - `__shared__ float scores[32][32]` (4KB) - Each thread computes several elements of scores 5. Apply causal mask: set to -inf where j > i 6. Compute softmax over each row - First find max per row - Then compute exp and sum - Then normalize 7. Compute output = scores @ V - Output is (32, 64) Wait, but if I need to apply causal mask, only positions where j <= i are valid. For row i, columns i+1 to 31 are masked. For softmax, after masking: - exp(masked_value) ≈ 0 - So it doesn't contribute to the sum With shared memory already at 36KB, can I run on H100? H100 has 228KB per SM. Yes, 36KB is well within limits. Let me refine the kernel: ```cuda __global__ void bart_attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, float* __restrict__ out, int B, int H, int S, int Dh ) { int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; if (b >= B || h >= H) return; // Each block processes one (b, h) int qkv_stride = H * S * Dh; int head_stride = S * Dh; const float* q_ptr = q + b * qkv_stride + h * head_stride; const float* k_ptr = k + b * qkv_stride + h * head_stride; const float* v_ptr = v + b * qkv_stride + h * head_stride; float* o_ptr = out + b * qkv_stride + h * head_stride; __shared__ float q_sm[32][64]; __shared__ float k_sm[32][64]; __shared__ float v_sm[32][64]; __shared__ float scores[32][32]; __shared__ float max_vals[32]; __shared__ float sum_exp[32]; // Load Q, K, V for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * Dh; i += blockDim.x) { int pos = i / Dh; int d = i % Dh; q_sm[pos][d] = q_ptr[i]; k_sm[pos][d] = k_ptr[i]; v_sm[pos][d] = v_ptr[i]; } __syncthreads(); // Compute Q @ K^T float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)Dh); for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { int i = idx / S; int j = idx % S; if (j > i) { scores[i][j] = -1e9f; // causal mask } else { float dot = 0.0f; for (int d = 0; d < Dh; d++) { dot += q_sm[i][d] * k_sm[j][d]; } scores[i][j] = dot * scale; } } __syncthreads(); // Softmax per row for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S; i += blockDim.x) { float max_val = scores[i][0]; for (int j = 1; j <= i; j++) { if (scores[i][j] > max_val) max_val = scores[i][j]; } max_vals[i] = max_val; } __syncthreads(); for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { int i = idx / S; int j = idx % S; if (j <= i) { scores[i][j] = expf(scores[i][j] - max_vals[i]); } } __syncthreads(); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S; i += blockDim.x) { float sum = 0.0f; for (int j = 0; j <= i; j++) { sum += scores[i][j]; } sum_exp[i] = sum; } __syncthreads(); for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x) { int i = idx / S; int j = idx % S; if (j <= i) { scores[i][j] /= sum_exp[i]; } } __syncthreads(); // Compute scores @ V for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * Dh; idx += blockDim.x) { int i = idx / Dh; int d = idx % Dh; float val = 0.0f; for (int j = 0; j <= i; j++) { val += scores[i][j] * v_sm[j][d]; } o_ptr[idx] = val; } } ``` Wait, for S=32 and Dh=64, this kernel should be correct. But is it fast? - Q @ K^T with manual inner loop over Dh=64: 32*32*64 = 65K FMAs per block - Score @ V: 32*64*32 = 65K FMAs per block - Total: ~130K FMAs per block For 16384 blocks, total FMAs: ~2.1B FMAs = 4.2 GFLOPs (each FMA is 2 FLOPs) Wait, 130K * 16384 = 2.13B FMAs = 4.26 GFLOPs. At 67 TFLOPS FP32, this would take ~0.06ms for the attention computation. But in practice, with shared memory loads and thread divergence (especially in the loops with `j <= i`), it might be slower. Thread divergence: in the `for (int j = 0; j <= i; j++)` loops, different threads have different loop bounds, causing divergence. For S=32, this is actually not too bad since the warp size is 32. But for 256 threads, threads within a warp might diverge. Actually, for `int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < S * S; idx += blockDim.x`, threads within the same warp will have similar `i` values (since idx increments by 256, and warp has 32 threads, threads in a warp span 32 consecutive idx values, which might span different rows). Hmm, maybe 256 threads is too many. What about 32 threads? Then each thread handles one row, and there's no divergence in the dot products within a warp... but actually each thread would do a lot of sequential work. Let me reconsider. For the dot product `dot += q_sm[i][d] * k_sm[j][d]`, if the threads are computing different (i, j) pairs, there's no divergence because the Dh loop is the same for all threads. For softmax and the final output, divergence occurs because different rows have different number of valid elements. But since S=32 is small, maybe it's fine. But with softmax, both should effectively zero out the masked positions. However, for exact numerical matching, I should use the same mask value. Then `mask_cond < column_vector` creates a matrix where position (i, j) is True if j < i + 1, i.e., j <= i. So the upper triangle (j > i) is False, and those positions keep the `-inf` value. Oh wait, I had the logic reversed. `mask_cond` is a row vector [0, 1, 2, ...]. `(mask_cond + 1).view(tgt_len, 1)` is a column vector [[1], [2], [3], ...]. Comparing `row < column`: - (0, 0): 0 < 1 -> True -> set to 0 - (0, 1): 1 < 1 -> False -> keep -inf - (1, 0): 0 < 2 -> True -> set to 0 - (1, 1): 1 < 2 -> True -> set to 0 - etc. So the True values (set to 0) are where j < i + 1, i.e., j <= i. This is exactly the lower triangle including diagonal. That makes sense! For my custom kernel, I'll set `scores[i][j] = 0` when `j <= i`, and `scores[i][j] = large_negative` when `j > i`. Now let me draft the exact code. ```python import torch from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline import math # C++ and CUDA source cpp_source = """ #include <torch/extension.h> #include <vector> // Custom attention kernel declaration at::Tensor bart_attention_cuda(const at::Tensor& q, const at::Tensor& k, const at::Tensor& v); at::Tensor bart_forward( at::Tensor input_ids, at::Tensor embed_tokens, at::Tensor embed_positions, double embed_scale, at::Tensor self_attn_layernorm_weights, at::Tensor self_attn_layernorm_biases, at::Tensor qkv_weights, at::Tensor qkv_biases, at::Tensor out_proj_weights, at::Tensor out_proj_biases, at::Tensor ffn_layernorm_weights, at::Tensor ffn_layernorm_biases, at::Tensor fc1_weights, at::Tensor fc1_biases, at::Tensor fc2_weights, at::Tensor fc2_biases, at::Tensor final_layernorm_weight, at::Tensor final_layernorm_bias, at::Tensor lm_head_weight, at::Tensor lm_head_bias, double eps ) { int B = input_ids.size(0); int S = input_ids.size(1); int D = embed_tokens.size(1); int num_layers = self_attn_layernorm_weights.size(0); int vocab_size = embed_tokens.size(0); // Embeddings auto inputs_embeds = at::embedding(embed_tokens, input_ids) * embed_scale; auto positions = at::arange(S, input_ids.options().dtype(at::kLong)); auto embed_pos = at::embedding(embed_positions, positions); auto hidden = inputs_embeds + embed_pos; // Causal mask (S, S) auto causal_mask = at::full({S, S}, -3.402823466e+38f, hidden.options()); auto mask_cond = at::arange(S, input_ids.options().dtype(at::kLong)); auto mask_comparison = mask_cond.unsqueeze(0) < (mask_cond + 1).unsqueeze(1); causal_mask = causal_mask.masked_fill(mask_comparison, 0.0f); for (int i = 0; i < num_layers; i++) { // Self attention auto residual = hidden; auto ln_w = self_attn_layernorm_weights[i]; auto ln_b = self_attn_layernorm_biases[i]; auto normed = at::native_layer_norm(hidden, {D}, ln_w, ln_b, eps)[0]; auto qkv_w = qkv_weights[i]; auto qkv_b = qkv_biases[i]; auto qkv = at::addmm(qkv_b, normed, qkv_w.t()); auto q = qkv.narrow(-1, 0, D); auto k = qkv.narrow(-1, D, D); auto v = qkv.narrow(-1, 2*D, D); int num_heads = 16; // For BART-large, or infer from shapes int head_dim = D / num_heads; q = q.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); k = k.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); v = v.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); // Attention // auto scores = at::matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)) / std::sqrt(head_dim); // scores = scores + causal_mask.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(0); // scores = at::softmax(scores, -1); // auto attn = at::matmul(scores, v); // attn = attn.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({B, S, D}); // Or use custom kernel auto attn = bart_attention_cuda(q, k, v); auto out_w = out_proj_weights[i]; auto out_b = out_proj_biases[i]; auto out = at::addmm(out_b, attn, out_w.t()); hidden = residual + out; // FFN residual = hidden; auto ffn_ln_w = ffn_layernorm_weights[i]; auto ffn_ln_b = ffn_layernorm_biases[i]; normed = at::native_layer_norm(hidden, {D}, ffn_ln_w, ffn_ln_b, eps)[0]; auto fc1_w = fc1_weights[i]; auto fc1_b = fc1_biases[i]; auto ffn1 = at::addmm(fc1_b, normed, fc1_w.t()); ffn1 = at::gelu(ffn1); auto fc2_w = fc2_weights[i]; auto fc2_b = fc2_biases[i]; auto ffn2 = at::addmm(fc2_b, ffn1, fc2_w.t()); hidden = residual + ffn2; } // Final layer norm hidden = at::native_layer_norm(hidden, {D}, final_layernorm_weight, final_layernorm_bias, eps)[0]; // LM head auto logits = at::addmm(lm_head_bias, hidden, lm_head_weight.t()); return logits; } """ cuda_source = """ #include <torch/extension.h> __global__ void bart_attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, float* __restrict__ out, int B, int H, int S, int Dh ) { int b = blockIdx.x; This might be slow but acceptable. However, `load_inline` might have issues being called in `__init__` if it's not at module level. But actually, many PyTorch extension examples call it in `__init__` or at module load time. Let me check if there's an issue with compilation happening during the model evaluation. Actually, a better practice is to call `load_inline` at module load time (outside the class), so it compiles once when the module is imported. This avoids recompilation on every model instantiation. Also, `load_inline` creates a Python module with the compiled functions. Calling it in `__init__` should work, but there could be issues with the compilation happening in a temporary directory that gets cleaned up. It's safer to call it at module scope. But in memory, moving from one head to the next is moving by Dh elements in the last dim. However, in the original tensor, q occupies the first D elements of each (b, s) position. The stride between elements within q is 1. The "stride" between heads is Dh = 64. But if we look at the actual memory, after the last element of head h, the next element is the first element of head h+1. So s2 = 64, s1 = H * Dh = 1024. But wait, s1 in the original tensor is 3072, not 1024. Hmm, this is getting complicated. The point is that after `.reshape`, the tensor might or might not be contiguous, but after `.permute()`, it definitely is NOT contiguous. For `load_inline` at module scope: ```python import torch from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig _cuda_source = r""" #include <torch/extension.h> #include <tuple> #define FLOAT_MIN -3.402823466e+38f __global__ void bart_attn_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, float* __restrict__ out, int B, int H, int S, int Dh ) { int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; if (b >= B || h >= H) return; int stride_b = H * S * Dh; int stride_h = S * Dh; const float* q_ptr = q + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; const float* k_ptr = k + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; const float* v_ptr = v + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; float* o_ptr = out + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* q_sm = smem; float* k_sm = smem + S * Dh; float* v_sm = k_sm + S * Dh; float* score = v_sm + S * Dh; float* s_max = score + S * S; float* s_sum = s_max + S; for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * Dh; i += blockDim.x) { q_sm[i] = q_ptr[i]; k_sm[i] = k_ptr[i]; v_sm[i] = v_ptr[i]; } __syncthreads(); float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)Dh); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / S; int col = i % S; if (col > row) { score[i] = FLOAT_MIN; } else { float dot = 0.0f; for (int d = 0; d < Dh; d++) { dot += q_sm[row * Dh + d] * k_sm[col * Dh + d]; } score[i] = dot * scale; } } __syncthreads(); for (int * S; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / S; int col = i % S; if (col <= row) { score[i] /= s_sum[row]; } } __syncthreads(); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * Dh; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / Dh; int at::Tensor& k, const at::Tensor& v) { int B = q.size(0); int H = q.size(1); int S = q.size(2); int Dh = q.size(3); auto out = at::zeros_like(q); dim3 grid(B, H); int threads = 256; int smem_size = (3 * S * Dh + S * S + 2 * S) * sizeof(float); bart_attn_kernel<<<grid, threads, smem_size>>>( q.data_ptr<float>(), k.data_ptr<float>(), v.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, S, Dh ); return out; } at::Tensor bart_forward( at::Tensor input_ids, at::Tensor embed_tokens, at::Tensor embed_positions, double embed_scale, at::Tensor self_attn_ln_w, at::Tensor self_attn_ln_b, at::Tensor qkv_w, at::Tensor qkv_b, at::Tensor out_w, at::Tensor out_b, at::Tensor ffn_ln_w, at::Tensor ffn_ln_b, at::Tensor fc1_w, at::Tensor fc1_b, at::Tensor fc2_w, at::Tensor fc2_b, at::Tensor final_ln_w, at::Tensor final_ln_b, at::Tensor lm_head_w, at::Tensor lm_head_b, double eps, int64_t num_heads ) { int B = input_ids.size(0); int S = input_ids.size(1); int D = embed_tokens.size(1); int num_layers = self_attn_ln_w.size(0); auto inputs_embeds = at::embedding(embed_tokens, input_ids) * embed_scale; auto positions = at::arange(S, input_ids.options().dtype(at::kLong)); auto embed_pos = at::embedding(embed_positions, positions); auto hidden = inputs_embeds + embed_pos; auto causal_mask = at::full({S, S}, FLOAT_MIN, hidden.options()); auto mask_cond = at::arange(S, input_ids.options().dtype(at::kLong)); auto mask_cmp = mask_cond.unsqueeze(0) < (mask_cond + 1).unsqueeze(1); causal_mask = causal_mask.masked_fill(mask_cmp, 0.0f); int head_dim = D / num_heads; for (int i = 0; i < num_layers; i++) { auto residual = hidden; auto normed = at::layer_norm(hidden, {D}, self_attn_ln_w[i], self_attn_ln_b[i], eps, true); auto qkv = at::addmm(qkv_b[i], normed, qkv_w[i].t()); auto q = qkv.narrow(-1, 0, D); auto k = qkv.narrow(-1, D, D); auto v = qkv.narrow(-1, 2 * D, D); q = q.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).contiguous(); k = k.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).contiguous(); v = v.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).contiguous(); auto attn = bart_attention_cuda(q, k, v); attn = attn.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({B, S, D}); auto out_proj = at::addmm(out_b[i], attn, out_w[i].t()); hidden = residual + out_proj; residual = hidden; normed = at::layer_norm(hidden, {D}, ffn_ln_w[i], ffn_ln_b[i], eps, true); auto ffn1 = at::addmm(fc1_b[i], normed, fc1_w[i].t()); ffn1 = at::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = at::addmm(fc2_b[i], ffn1, fc2_w[i].t()); hidden = residual + ffn2; } hidden = at::layer_norm(hidden, {D}, final_ln_w, final_ln_b, eps, true); auto logits = at::addmm(lm_head_b, hidden, lm_head_w.t()); return logits; } """ _bart_cuda = None class num_layers = config.decoder_layers d_model = config.d_model embed_scale = float(decoder.embed_scale if hasattr(decoder, 'embed_scale') else 1.0) embed_tokens = decoder.embed_tokens.weight lm_head_b is None: lm_head_b = torch.zeros(config.vocab_size, device=lm_head_w.device, dtype=lm_head_w.dtype) if hasattr(model, 'final_logits_bias'): lm_head_b = lm_head_b + model.final_logits_bias.squeeze(0) self_attn_ln_w = [] self_attn_ln_b = [] qkv_w = [] qkv_b = [] out_w = [] out_b = [] ffn_ln_w = [] ffn_ln_b = [] fc1_w = [] fc1_b = [] fc2_w = [] fc2_b = [] for i in range(num_layers): layer = decoder.layers[i] self_attn_ln_w.append(layer.self_attn_layer_norm.weight) self_attn_ln_b.append(layer.self_attn_layer_norm.bias) q_w = layer.self_attn.q_proj.weight k_w = layer.self_attn.k_proj.weight v_w = layer.self_attn.v_proj.weight qkv_w.append(torch.cat([q_w, k_w, v_w], dim=0)) q_b = layer.self_attn.q_proj.bias k_b = layer.self_attn.k_proj.bias v_b = layer.self_attn.v_proj.bias qkv_b.append(torch.cat([q_b, k_b, v_b], dim=0)) out_w.append(layer.self_attn.out_proj.weight) out_b.append(layer.self_attn.out_proj.bias) ffn_ln_w.append(layer.final_layer_norm.weight) ffn_ln_b.append(layer.final_layer_norm.bias) fc1_w.append(layer.fc1.weight) fc1_b.append(layer.fc1.bias) fc2_w.append(layer.fc2.weight) fc2_b.append(layer.fc2.bias) stack = lambda x: torch.stack(x, dim=0) self.register_buffer('embed_tokens', embed_tokens) self.register_buffer('embed_positions', embed_positions) self.register_buffer('final_ln_w', final_ln_w) self.register_buffer('final_ln_b', final_ln_b) self.register_buffer('lm_head_w', lm_head_w) self.register_buffer('lm_head_b', lm_head_b) self.register_buffer('self_attn_ln_w', stack(self_attn_ln_w)) self.register_buffer('self_attn_ln_b', stack(self_attn_ln_b)) self.register_buffer('qkv_w', stack(qkv_w)) self.register_buffer('qkv_b', stack(qkv_b)) self.register_buffer('out_w', stack(out_w)) self.register_buffer('out_b', stack(out_b)) self.register_buffer('ffn_ln_w', stack(ffn_ln_w)) self.register_buffer('ffn_ln_b', stack(ffn_ln_b)) self.register_buffer('fc1_w', stack(fc1_w)) self.register_buffer('fc1_b', stack(fc1_b)) self.register_buffer('fc2_w', stack(fc2_w)) self.register_buffer('fc2_b', stack(fc2_b)) self.embed_scale = embed_scale self.num_heads = config.decoder_attention_heads self.eps = decoder.layers[0].self_attn_layer_norm.eps global _bart_cuda if _bart_cuda is None: _bart_cuda = load_inline( name="bart_forward", cpp_sources="", cuda_sources=_cuda_source, functions=["bart_forward"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"], verbose=False, ) def forward(self, x): return _bart_cuda.bart_forward( x, self.embed_tokens, self.embed_positions, self.embed_scale, self.self_attn_ln_w, self.self_attn_ln_b, self.qkv_w, self.qkv_b, self.out_w, self.out_b, self.ffn_ln_w, OK, the complete code: ```python import torch from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig CUDA_SOURCE = r""" #include <torch/extension.h> #include <vector> #include <cmath> #define FLOAT_MIN -3.402823466e+38f __global__ void bart_attn_kernel( const float* __restrict__ q, const float* __restrict__ k, const float* __restrict__ v, float* __restrict__ out, int B, int H, int S, int Dh ) { int b = blockIdx.x; int h = blockIdx.y; if (b >= B || h >= H) return; int stride_b = H * S * Dh; int stride_h = S * Dh; const float* q_ptr = q + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; const float* k_ptr = k + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; const float* v_ptr = v + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; float* o_ptr = out + b * stride_b + h * stride_h; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* q_sm = smem; float* k_sm = smem + S * Dh; float* v_sm = k_sm + S * Dh; float* score = v_sm + S * Dh; float* s_max = score + S * S; float* s_sum = s_max + S; for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * Dh; i += blockDim.x) { q_sm[i] = q_ptr[i]; k_sm[i] = k_ptr[i]; v_sm[i] = v_ptr[i]; } __syncthreads(); float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)Dh); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / S; int col = i % S; if (col > row) { score[i] = FLOAT_MIN; } else { float dot = 0.0f; for (int d = 0; d < Dh; d++) { dot += q_sm[row * Dh + d] * k_sm[col * Dh + d]; } score[i] = dot * scale; } } __syncthreads(); for (int row = threadIdx.x; row < S; row += blockDim.x) { float mx = score[row * S]; for (int col = 1; col <= row; col++) { float val = score[row * S + col]; if (val > mx) mx = val; } s_max[row] = mx; } __syncthreads(); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / S; int col = i % S; if (col <= row) { score[i] = expf(score[i] - s_max[row]); } } __syncthreads(); for (int row = threadIdx.x; row < S; row += blockDim.x) { float sum = 0.0f; for (int col = 0; col <= row; col++) { sum += score[row * S + col]; } s_sum[row] = sum; } __syncthreads(); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * S; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / S; int col = i % S; if (col <= row) { score[i] /= s_sum[row]; } } __syncthreads(); for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < S * Dh; i += blockDim.x) { int row = i / Dh; int d = i % Dh; float val = 0.0f; for (int col = 0; col <= row; col++) { val += score[row * S + col] * v_sm[col * Dh + d]; } o_ptr[i] = val; } } at::Tensor bart_attention_cuda(const at::Tensor& q, const at::Tensor& k, const at::Tensor& v) { int B = q.size(0); int H = q.size(1); int S = q.size(2); int Dh = q.size(3); auto out = at::zeros_like(q); dim3 grid(B, H); int threads = 256; int smem_size = (3 * S * Dh + S * S + 2 * S) * sizeof(float); bart_attn_kernel<<<grid, threads, smem_size>>>( q.data_ptr<float>(), k.data_ptr<float>(), v.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, S, Dh ); return out; } at::Tensor bart_forward( at::Tensor input_ids, at::Tensor embed_tokens, at::Tensor embed_positions, double embed_scale, const std::vector<at::Tensor>& layer_params, const std::vector<at::Tensor>& head_params, double eps, int64_t num_heads ) { int B = input_ids.size(0); int S = input_ids.size(1); int D = embed_tokens.size(1); auto self_attn_ln_w = layer_params[0]; auto self_attn_ln_b = layer_params[1]; auto qkv_w = layer_params[2]; auto qkv_b = layer_params[3]; auto out_w = layer_params[4]; auto out_b = layer_params[5]; auto ffn_ln_w = layer_params[6]; auto ffn_ln_b = layer_params[7]; auto fc1_w = layer_params[8]; auto fc1_b = layer_params[9]; auto fc2_w = layer_params[10]; auto fc2_b = layer_params[11]; auto final_ln_w = head_params[0]; auto final_ln_b = head_params[1]; auto lm_head_w = head_params[2]; auto lm_head_b = head_params[3]; int num_layers = self_attn_ln_w.size(0); int head_dim = D / num_heads; auto inputs_embeds = at::embedding(embed_tokens, input_ids) * embed_scale; auto positions = at::arange(S, input_ids.options().dtype(at::kLong)); auto embed_pos = at::embedding(embed_positions, positions); auto hidden = inputs_embeds + embed_pos; auto causal_mask = at::full({S, S}, FLOAT_MIN, hidden.options()); auto mask_cond = at::arange(S, input_ids.options().dtype(at::kLong)); auto mask_cmp = mask_cond.unsqueeze(0) < (mask_cond + 1).unsqueeze(1); causal_mask = causal_mask.masked_fill(mask_cmp, 0.0f); for (int i = 0; i < num_layers; i++) { auto residual = hidden; auto normed = at::layer_norm(hidden, {D}, self_attn_ln_w[i], self_attn_ln_b[i], eps, true); auto qkv = at::addmm(qkv_b[i], normed, qkv_w[i].t()); auto q = qkv.narrow(-1, 0, D); auto k = qkv.narrow(-1, D, D); auto v = qkv.narrow(-1, 2 * D, D); q = q.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).contiguous(); k = k.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).contiguous(); v = v.reshape({B, S, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).contiguous(); auto attn = bart_attention_cuda(q, k, v); attn = attn.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({B, S, D}); auto out_proj = at::addmm(out_b[i], attn, out_w[i].t()); hidden = residual + out_proj; residual = hidden; normed = at::layer_norm(hidden, {D}, ffn_ln_w[i], ffn_ln_b[i], eps, true); auto ffn1 = at::addmm(fc1_b[i], normed, fc1_w[i].t()); ffn1 = at::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = at::addmm(fc2_b[i], ffn1, fc2_w[i].t()); hidden = residual + ffn2; } hidden = at::layer_norm(hidden, {D}, final_ln_w, final_ln_b, eps, true); auto logits = at::addmm(lm_head_b, hidden, lm_head_w.t()); return logits; } """ _bart_ext = None class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, model_name, config): super().__init__() model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, config=config) model.eval() decoder = model.model.decoder num_layers = config.decoder_layers d_model = config.d_model embed_scale = float(decoder.embed_scale if hasattr(decoder, 'embed_scale') else 1.0) embed_tokens = decoder.embed_tokens.weight embed_positions = decoder.embed_positions.weight final_ln_w = decoder.layer_norm.weight final_ln_b = decoder.layer_norm.bias lm_head_w = model.lm_head.weight lm_head_b = model.lm_head.bias if lm_head_b is None: lm_head_b = torch.zeros(config.vocab_size, device=lm_head_w.device, dtype=lm_head_w.dtype) if hasattr(model, 'final_logits_bias'): lm_head_b = lm_head_b + model.final_logits_bias.squeeze(0) self_attn_ln_w = [] self_attn_ln_b = [] qkv_w = [] qkv_b = [] out_w = [] out_b = [] ffn_ln_w = [] ffn_ln_b = [] fc1_w = [] fc1_b = [] fc2_w = [] fc2_b = [] for i in range(num_layers): layer = decoder.layers[i] self_attn_ln_w.append(layer.self_attn_layer_norm.weight) self_attn_ln_b.append(layer.self_attn_layer_norm.bias) q_w = layer.self_attn.q_proj.weight k_w = layer.self_attn.k_proj.weight v_w = layer.self_attn.v_proj.weight qkv_w.append(torch.cat([q_w, k_w, v_w], dim=0)) q_b = layer.self_attn.q_proj.bias k_b = layer.self_attn.k_proj.bias v_b = layer.self_attn.v_proj.bias qkv_b.append(torch.cat([q_b, k_b, v_b], dim=0)) out_w.append(layer.self_attn.out_proj.weight) out_b.append(layer.self_attn.out_proj.bias) ffn_ln_w.append(layer.final_layer_norm.weight) ffn_ln_b.append(layer.final_layer_norm.bias) fc1_w.append(layer.fc1.weight) fc1_b.append(layer.fc1.bias) fc2_w.append(layer.fc2.weight) fc2_b.append(layer.fc2.bias) stack = lambda x: torch.stack(x, dim=0) self.register_buffer('embed_tokens', embed_tokens) self.register_buffer('embed_positions', embed_positions) self.register_buffer('final_ln_w', final_ln_w) self.register_buffer('final_ln_b', final_ln_b) self.register_buffer('lm_head_w', lm_head_w) self.register_buffer('lm_head_b', lm_head_b) self.register_buffer('self_attn_ln_w', stack(self_attn_ln_w)) self.register_buffer('self_attn_ln_b', stack(self_attn_ln_b)) self.register_buffer('qkv_w', stack(qkv_w)) self.register_buffer('qkv_b', stack(qkv_b)) self.register_buffer('out_w', stack(out_w)) self.register_buffer('out_b', stack(out_b)) self.register_buffer('ffn_ln_w', stack(ffn_ln_w)) self.register_buffer('ffn_ln_b', stack(ffn_ln_b)) self.register_buffer('fc1_w', stack(fc1_w)) self.register_buffer('fc1_b', stack(fc1_b)) self.register_buffer('fc2_w', stack(fc2_w)) self.register_buffer('fc2_b', stack(fc2_b)) self.embed_scale = embed_scale self.num_heads = config.decoder_attention_heads self.eps = decoder.layers[0].self_attn_layer_norm.eps global _bart_ext if _bart_ext is None: _bart_ext = load_inline( name="bart_forward_ext", cpp_sources="", cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE, functions=["bart_forward"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"], verbose=False, ) def forward(self, x): layer_params = [ self.self_attn_ln_w, self.self_attn_ln_b, self.lm_head_b] return _bart_ext.bart_forward( x, self.embed_tokens, self.embed_positions, self.embed_scale, layer_params, head_params, self.eps, self.num_heads ) ``` This looks quite complete. In my code, I use `model.lm_head.weight` and `model.lm_head.bias`, which should work. And `model.final_logits_bias` should exist. I noticed in my C++ code, I use `at::layer_norm` with the weight and bias parameters. But `at::layer_norm` might not exist in the `at` namespace in some PyTorch versions. It might be `torch::layer_norm`. Let me check... In PyTorch C++ API, `torch::nn::functional::layer_norm` is a C++ functional equivalent. But `at::layer_norm` is the ATen native function. Both should exist. If `at::layer_norm` doesn't work, I can fall back to manual implementation: ```cpp auto mean = x.mean({-1}, true); auto var = x.var({-1}, false, true); auto y = (x - mean) / (var + eps).sqrt(); y = y * w + b; ``` But `at::layer_norm` should be more optimized and likely to match exactly. Actually, wait. `x.var({-1}, false, true)` - is this the correct C++ API? In Python it's `x.var(dim=-1, unbiased=False, keepdim=True)`. In C++: ```cpp Tensor var(IntArrayRef dim, bool unbiased, bool keepdim) const; ``` So `x.var({-1}, false, true)` should work. But we need to pass `IntArrayRef`. `-1` as a dimension in a list: `{-1}` creates a `std::initializer_list<int64_t>`. Actually, `x.var(-1, false, true)` might also work with scalar dim. But to be safe, `{ -1 }` is better. OK, I just realized `at::Tensor::var` has a `dim` parameter of type `IntArrayRef` or similar. Let me use the explicit overload. Actually, looking at ATen, `var` has multiple overloads: ```cpp Tensor var(c10::optional<IntArrayRef> dim=c10::nullopt, bool unbiased=true, bool keepdim=false) const; ``` But wait, if `dim` is optional and I pass `{-1}`, it should work. However, for layer normalization, the exact formula used by PyTorch might be slightly different from my manual `mean`, `var`, `(x - mean) / sqrt(var + eps)` approach. For instance, PyTorch might compute the mean and variance in a fused kernel, or use Welford's algorithm for numerical stability. The results should be the same within floating-point rounding, but using `at::layer_norm` is safer. Alright, I'll use `at::layer_norm` and see if it compiles. Let me now actually compose the final code string to pass to the compile tool. Wait, I want to add one small optimization. In the custom attention kernel, instead of `expf` and `sqrtf`, I can use `__expf` and `__fsqrt_rn` for faster intrinsic functions. But with `-O3 --use_fast_math`, the compiler should do this automatically. I'll keep the explicit names for readability. Also, the shared memory calculation: `smem_size = (3 * S * Dh + S * S + 2 * S) * sizeof(float)`. For S=32, Dh=64: `3 * 32 * 64 = 6144`, `32 * 32 = 1024`, `2 * 32 = 64`, total = `7232` floats. `7232 * 4 = 28928` bytes ≈ 28.3 KB. This is under the 48KB default shared memory limit on most GPUs, and well under the 228KB on H100. Actually, the default shared memory limit per block is 48KB on many GPUs, but on H100 it's higher (up to 228KB). With `-Xptxas -v`, we can see if it exceeds limits. For sm_90 (H100), the dynamic shared memory limit might be different, but 28KB should be fine. One more thing: `load_inline` might not support empty `cpp_sources`. Let me check. That should be fine. Actually, let me look more closely at `load_inline` behavior. From the PyTorch source, `load_inline` creates a temporary directory, writes the sources to files, and then calls `load`. If `cpp_sources` is a string, it writes it to a `.cpp` file. If `cuda_sources` is provided, it writes to a `.cu` file. Then `load` compiles them with the appropriate compiler and links them. If `cpp_sources` is an empty string, it still creates an empty `.cpp` file, which might compile or might cause issues. Also, one concern: I need to make sure that my attention mask is correct. In BART decoder, self attention is causal-like but uses a triangular mask - I was handling the standard upper-triangular masking. However, for the bart decoder, there's another key factor: it uses `decoder_attention_mask` and `causal_mask` together. Since we only have `input_ids` with no explicit padding mask, all positions should be valid. But the causal mask should prevent attending to future positions. Let me run correctness first.
